&lt;td width=10%&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;NOTE 2:&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;td width=90%&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;DESCRIPTION OF THE BUSINESS AND SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;/table&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Description of Business&lt;/font&gt;&amp;#160;- Tofutti Brands Inc. (&amp;#8220;Tofutti&amp;#8221; or the &amp;#8220;Company&amp;#8221;) is engaged in one business segment
 the development
 production and marketing of non-dairy frozen desserts and other food products.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Operating Segments.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&amp;#160;The Company reports on operating segments in accordance with standards for public&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;companies&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&amp;#160;to report information about operating segments and geographic distribution of sales in financial statements.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;While the Company has multiple products and or product groups
 its goal is to focus on non-dairy foods.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;The Company&amp;#8217;s chief operating decision maker tracks revenue by product groups
 but does not track more granular operating results by product group as many of the ingredients are similar amongst these groups.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;As a result
 the Company has determined that it has only one operating segment
 which is the development
 production and marketing of soy-based
&amp;#160;&amp;#160;non-dairy frozen desserts
 frozen food products and soy-based cheese products.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Fiscal Year&lt;/font&gt;&amp;#160;- The Company operates on a fiscal year ending on the Saturday closest to December 31st.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;Fiscal years for the financial statements included herein are the fifty-two week fiscal periods ended on December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013
 respectively.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Estimates and Uncertainties&lt;/font&gt;&amp;#160;- The preparation of the financial statements in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting period.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;Significant estimates include allowance for doubtful accounts
 sales promotion accruals
 inventory reserves and reserves for uncertain tax positions.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;Actual results could differ from those estimates.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Revenue Recognition&lt;/font&gt;&amp;#160;- Revenue is recognized when goods are shipped from production facilities or outside warehouses to customers. Revenue is recognized when the following four criteria under ASC 605&amp;#160;&amp;#160;have been met: the product has been shipped and the Company has no significant remaining obligations; persuasive evidence of an arrangement exists; the price to the buyer is fixed or determinable; and collection is probable.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;Deductions from sales for promotional programs
 manufacturers&amp;#8217; charge-backs
 co-operative advertising programs and other programs are recorded as reductions of revenues and are provided for at the time of initial sale of product. Freight charged to customers is included in revenues
 and has generally been insignificant.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Concentration of Credit/Sales Risk&lt;/font&gt;&amp;#160;- Financial instruments that potentially subject the Company to concentration of credit risk consist primarily of cash and unsecured trade receivables.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;During the year
 the Company&amp;#8217;s cash balance at its financial institution exceeded the FDIC limit of $250.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;The Company performs ongoing evaluations of its customers&amp;#8217; financial condition and does not require collateral.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;Management feels that credit risk beyond the established allowances at December 27
 2014 is limited.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;During the fiscal years ended December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013
 the Company derived approximately 83% and 84%
 respectively
 of its net sales domestically.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;The remaining sales in both periods were exports to foreign countries.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;The accounts receivable balance of one customer represented approximately 16% of total accounts receivable at December 27
 2014
 and two customers represented a combined 25% of total accounts receivable at December 28
 2013. In addition
 a significant portion of the Company&amp;#8217;s sales are to several key distributors
 which are large distribution companies with numerous divisions and subsidiaries who act independently. Such distributors as a group accounted for 43% and 45% of the Company&amp;#8217;s net sales for the fiscal years ended December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Accounts Receivable -&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;The majority of the Company&amp;#8217;s accounts receivables are due from distributors (domestic and international) and retailers.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;Credit is extended based on evaluation of a customers&amp;#8217; financial condition and
 generally
 collateral is not required. Accounts receivable are most often due within 30 to 90 days and are stated at amounts due from customers net of an allowance for doubtful accounts. Accounts outstanding longer than the contractual payment terms are considered past due. The Company determines its allowance by considering a number of factors
 including the length of time trade accounts receivable are past due
 the Company&amp;#8217;s previous loss history
 the customer&amp;#8217;s current ability to pay its obligation to the Company
 and the condition of the general economy and the industry as a whole. The Company writes-off accounts receivable when they become uncollectible
 and payments subsequently received on such receivables are credited to the bad debt expense. The Company does not accrue interest on accounts receivable past due.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Deferred Revenue and Deferred Costs&lt;/font&gt;&amp;#160;- Deferred revenue represents amounts from sales of the Company&amp;#8217;s product that have been billed and shipped
 but for which the transactions have not met its revenue recognition criteria.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;The cost of the related product has been recorded as deferred costs on its balance sheet.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Cash and Cash Equivalents&lt;/font&gt;&amp;#160;- The Company considers all highly liquid investments with original maturities of three months or less to be cash equivalents.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Inventories&lt;/font&gt;&amp;#160;- Inventory is stated at lower of cost or market determined by first in first out (FIFO) method.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;Inventories in excess of future demand are written down and charged to the provision for inventories.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;At the point of which loss is recognized
 a new
 lower cost basis for that inventory is established and subsequent changes in facts and circumstances do not result in the restoration or increase in the newly established cost basis.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;The Company purchased approximately 26% and 27% of its finished products from one supplier and 28% and 28% of its finished products from another supplier during the periods ended&amp;#160;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;December 27
 2014&amp;#160;&amp;#160;and December 28
 2013&lt;/font&gt;
 respectively.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Income Taxes&lt;/font&gt;&amp;#160;- Deferred tax assets and liabilities are recognized for the future tax consequences attributable to differences between the financial statement carrying amounts of existing assets and liabilities and their respective tax bases.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;Deferred tax assets and liabilities are measured using enacted tax rates expected to apply to taxable income in the years in which those temporary differences are expected to be recovered or settled.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;The effect on deferred tax assets and liabilities of a change in tax rates is recognized in income in the period that includes the enactment date.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;A valuation allowance is recorded if there is uncertainty as to the realization of deferred tax assets. The Company will recognize a tax benefit in the financial statements for an uncertain tax position only if management&amp;#8217;s assessment is that the position is &amp;#8220;more likely than not&amp;#8221; (i.e.
 a likelihood greater than 50 percent) to be allowed by the tax jurisdiction based solely on the technical merits of the position. The term &amp;#8220;tax position&amp;#8221; refers to a position in a previously filed tax return or a position expected to be taken in a future tax return that is reflected in measuring current or deferred income tax assets and liabilities for financial reporting purposes.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Net Income Per Share&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;- Basic earnings per common share has been computed by dividing net income by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;Diluted earnings per share has been computed by dividing net income by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding
 including the dilutive effects of stock options.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;

 which primarily consist of cash and equivalents
 accounts receivable and accounts payable are stated at their carrying values.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;The carrying amounts approximate fair value because of the short-term nature of those instruments.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

099 during the fiscal years ended December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013
 respectively.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;Such costs are included in costs of goods sold.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

 2014 and December 28
 2013
 respectively.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Product Development Costs&lt;/font&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-style: italic; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;-&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;Costs of new product development and product redesign are charged to expense as incurred. Product development costs amounted to $641 and $585 during the fiscal years ended December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013
 respectively.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;Recent Accounting Pronouncements -&lt;/font&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; font-style: italic; font-weight: bold; display: inline;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;In May
 2014
 the FASB issued an accounting standards update that completes the joint effort by the FASB and International Accounting Standards Board to improve financial reporting by creating common revenue recognition guidance for GAAP and International Financial Reporting Standards. The update applies to all companies that enter into contracts with customers to transfer goods or services and is effective for Tofutti for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after December 15
 2015. Early application is not permitted and companies have the choice to apply the update either retrospectively to each reporting period presented or by recognizing the cumulative effect of applying the update at the date of initial application (January 1
 2017) and not adjusting comparative information. The Company is currently evaluating the requirements of this update and has not yet determined its impact on its financial statements.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;In August
 2014
 the FASB issued guidance that requires management to evaluate whether there are conditions or events that raise substantial doubt about an entity&amp;#8217;s ability to continue as a going concern. If such conditions or events exist
 disclosures are required that enable users of the financial statements to understand the nature of the conditions or events
 management&amp;#8217;s evaluation of the circumstances and management&amp;#8217;s plans to mitigate the conditions or events that raise substantial doubt about the entity&amp;#8217;s ability to continue as a going concern. The Company will be required to perform an annual assessment of its ability to continue as a going concern when this standard becomes effective for it on October 1
 2017; however
 the adoption of this guidance is not expected to impact the Company&amp;#8217;s financial position

&lt;div style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;On June 10
 2014
 the shareholders of the Company approved the 2014 Equity Incentive Plan (the &amp;#8220;2014 Plan&amp;#8221;). The 2014 Plan provides for grants of various types of awards that are designed to attract and retain highly qualified personnel who will contribute to the success of the Company and to provide incentives to participants in the 2014 Plan that are linked directly to increases in shareholder value which will therefore inure to the benefit of all shareholders of the Company. The Company intends to rely on a combination of multi-year performance awards
 options and other stock-based awards for these purposes.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;The 2014 Plan made 250
000 shares of Common Stock available for awards. The 2014 Plan also permits performance-based 2014 awards paid under it to be tax deductible under Section 162(m) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986
 as amended
 as &amp;#8220;performance-based compensation.&amp;#8221;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;

 and no options were outstanding as of year-end
 December 27
 2014 and December 28


&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;

 New Jersey.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;The 6
200 square foot facility houses its administrative offices
 a warehouse
 walk-in freezer and refrigerator
 and a product development laboratory and test kitchen.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;The Company&amp;#8217;s original lease agreement expired on July 1
 1999
 but it continues to occupy the premises under the terms of that agreement.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;Any changes by either the landlord or the Company remains subject to a six month notification period. The Company currently has no plans to enter into a long-term lease agreement for the facility. Rent expense was $80 in 2014 and $81 in 2013.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;The Company&amp;#8217;s management believes that the Cranford facility will continue to satisfy its space requirements for the foreseeable future and that if necessary

 a likelihood greater than 50 percent) to be allowed by the tax jurisdiction based solely on the technical merits of the position.  the Company&amp;#8217;s cash balance at its financial institution exceeded the FDIC limit of $250.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;The Company performs ongoing evaluations of its customers&amp;#8217; financial condition and does not require collateral.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;Management feels that credit risk beyond the established allowances at December 27
 2014 is limited.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=justify style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left style=font: 13.33px/normal 'times new roman', times, serif; color: #000000; text-transform: none; text-indent: 0pt; letter-spacing: normal; margin-right: 0pt; margin-left: 0pt; word-spacing: 0px; display: block; white-space: normal; widows: 1; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: 'times new roman'; font-size: 10pt; display: inline;&gt;During the fiscal years ended December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013
 the Company derived approximately 83% and 84%
 respectively
 of its net sales domestically.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;The remaining sales in both periods were exports to foreign countries.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;The accounts receivable balance of one customer represented approximately 16% of total accounts receivable at December 27
 2014
 and two customers represented a combined 25% of total accounts receivable at December 28
 2013. In addition
 a significant portion of the Company&amp;#8217;s sales are to several key distributors
 which are large distribution companies with numerous divisions and subsidiaries who act independently. Such distributors as a group accounted for 43% and 45% of the Company&amp;#8217;s net sales for the fiscal years ended December 27
 2014 and December 28


 generally
 collateral is not required. Accounts receivable are most often due within 30 to 90 days and are stated at amounts due from customers net of an allowance for doubtful accounts. Accounts outstanding longer than the contractual payment terms are considered past due. The Company determines its allowance by considering a number of factors
 including the length of time trade accounts receivable are past due
 the Company&amp;#8217;s previous loss history
 the customer&amp;#8217;s current ability to pay its obligation to the Company
 and the condition of the general economy and the industry as a whole. The Company writes-off accounts receivable when they become uncollectible





 a new
 lower cost basis for that inventory is established and subsequent changes in facts and circumstances do not result in the restoration or increase in the newly established cost basis.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

 2014&amp;#160;&amp;#160;and December 28

 2014
 the FASB issued an accounting standards update that completes the joint effort by the FASB and International Accounting Standards Board to improve financial reporting by creating common revenue recognition guidance for GAAP and International Financial Reporting Standards. The update applies to all companies that enter into contracts with customers to transfer goods or services and is effective for Tofutti for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after December 15
 2015. Early application is not permitted and companies have the choice to apply the update either retrospectively to each reporting period presented or by recognizing the cumulative effect of applying the update at the date of initial application (January 1
 2017) and not adjusting comparative information. The Company is currently evaluating the requirements of this update and has not yet determined its impact on its financial statements.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div align=left&gt;&lt;font style=font-family: times new roman,times; size=2&gt;In August
 2014
 the FASB issued guidance that requires management to evaluate whether there are conditions or events that raise substantial doubt about an entity&amp;#8217;s ability to continue as a going concern. If such conditions or events exist
 disclosures are required that enable users of the financial statements to understand the nature of the conditions or events
 management&amp;#8217;s evaluation of the circumstances and management&amp;#8217;s plans to mitigate the conditions or events that raise substantial doubt about the entity&amp;#8217;s ability to continue as a going concern. The Company will be required to perform an annual assessment of its ability to continue as a going concern when this standard becomes effective for it on October 1
 2017; however
 the adoption of this guidance is not expected to impact the Company&amp;#8217;s financial position

 its goal is to focus on non-dairy foods.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;The Company&amp;#8217;s chief operating decision maker tracks revenue by product groups
 but does not track more granular operating results by product group as many of the ingredients are similar amongst these groups.&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;As a result
 the Company has determined that it has only one operating segment
 which is the development

							function toggleNextSibling (e) {
							if (e.nextSibling.style.display=='none') {
							e.nextSibling.style.display='block';
							} else {
							e.nextSibling.style.display='none';
							}
							}

var Show = {};
Show.LastAR = null
Show.hideAR = function(){
	Show.LastAR.style.display = 'none';
};
Show.showAR = function ( link
 id
 win ){
	if( Show.LastAR ){
		Show.hideAR();
	}
	var ref = link;
	do {
		ref = ref.nextSibling;
	} while (ref && ref.nodeName != 'TABLE');
	if (!ref || ref.nodeName != 'TABLE') {
		var tmp = win ?
			win.document.getElementById(id) :
			document.getElementById(id);
		if( tmp ){
			ref = tmp.cloneNode(true);
			ref.id = '';
			link.parentNode.appendChild(ref);
		}
	}
	if( ref ){
		ref.style.display = 'block';
		Show.LastAR = ref;
	}
};
Show.toggleNext = function( link ){
	var ref = link;
	do{
		ref = ref.nextSibling;
	}while( ref.nodeName != 'DIV' );
	if( ref.style &&
		ref.style.display &&
		ref.style.display == 'none' ){
		ref.style.display = 'block';
		if( link.textContent ){
			link.textContent = link.textContent.replace( '+'
 '-' );
		}else{
			link.innerText = link.innerText.replace( '+'
 '-' );
		}
	}else{
		ref.style.display = 'none';
		if( link.textContent ){
			link.textContent = link.textContent.replace( '-'
 '+' );
		}else{
			link.innerText = link.innerText.replace( '-'
 '+' );
		}
	}
};











    
    
							function toggleNextSibling (e) {
							if (e.nextSibling.style.display=='none') {
							e.nextSibling.style.display='block';
							} else {
							e.nextSibling.style.display='none';
							}
							}
  
      

          

        

      






        
        


        
        






At December 27
 2014
 Tofutti Brands
 Inc. (the &#8220;Company&#8221;) had approximately $341 in cash compared to $214 at December 28
 2013.&#160;&#160;Net cash provided by operating activities for the year ended December 27
 2014 was $129 compared to $257 used in operating activities for the year ended December 28
 2013.&#160;&#160;Net cash provided by operating activities for the year ended December 27
 2014 was primarily the result of our net loss of $163
 which was offset by an increase in accounts payable and accrued liabilities of $295.

During the years ended December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013
 $2 and $0 was used in financing activities
 respectively.

The Company has historically financed operations and met capital requirements primarily through positive cash flow from operations.&#160;&#160;However
 due to the net loss for the year ended December 27
 2014 and cash used in operations
 the Company may require additional financing in order to accomplish or exceed their business plans for future periods.&#160;&#160;The Company is instituting additional cost cutting measures in fiscal year 2015 as a way to increase profitability in future periods.

The Company&#8217;s ability to introduce successful new products may be adversely affected by a number of factors
 such as unforeseen cost and expenses
 economic environment
 increased competition
 and other factors beyond the Company&#8217;s control.&#160;&#160;Management cannot provide assurance that the Company will operate profitably in the future
 or that it will not require significant additional financing in order to accomplish or exceed the objectives of its business plan.&#160;&#160;Consequently
 the Company&#8217;s historical operating results cannot be relied on to be an indicator of future performance
 and management cannot predict whether the Company will obtain or sustain positive operating cash flow or generate net income in the future.

&#160;The Company reports on operating segments in accordance with standards for public&#160;companies&#160;to report information about operating segments and geographic distribution of sales in financial statements.&#160;&#160;While the Company has multiple products and or product groups
 its goal is to focus on non-dairy foods.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s chief operating decision maker tracks revenue by product groups
 but does not track more granular operating results by product group as many of the ingredients are similar amongst these groups.&#160;&#160;&#160;As a result
 the Company has determined that it has only one operating segment
 which is the development
 production and marketing of soy-based
&#160;&#160;non-dairy frozen desserts
 frozen food products and soy-based cheese products.


        
&#160;- The Company operates on a fiscal year ending on the Saturday closest to December 31st.&#160;&#160;Fiscal years for the financial statements included herein are the fifty-two week fiscal periods ended on December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013
 respectively.


        
&#160;- The preparation of the financial statements in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting period.&#160;&#160;Significant estimates include allowance for doubtful accounts
 sales promotion accruals
 inventory reserves and reserves for uncertain tax positions.&#160;&#160;Actual results could differ from those estimates.


        
&#160;- Revenue is recognized when goods are shipped from production facilities or outside warehouses to customers. Revenue is recognized when the following four criteria under ASC 605&#160;&#160;have been met: the product has been shipped and the Company has no significant remaining obligations; persuasive evidence of an arrangement exists; the price to the buyer is fixed or determinable; and collection is probable.&#160;&#160;Deductions from sales for promotional programs
 manufacturers&#8217; charge-backs
 co-operative advertising programs and other programs are recorded as reductions of revenues and are provided for at the time of initial sale of product. Freight charged to customers is included in revenues
 and has generally been insignificant.


        
&#160;- Financial instruments that potentially subject the Company to concentration of credit risk consist primarily of cash and unsecured trade receivables.&#160;&#160;During the year
 the Company&#8217;s cash balance at its financial institution exceeded the FDIC limit of $250.

The Company performs ongoing evaluations of its customers&#8217; financial condition and does not require collateral.&#160;&#160;Management feels that credit risk beyond the established allowances at December 27
 2014 is limited.

During the fiscal years ended December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013
 the Company derived approximately 83% and 84%
 respectively
 of its net sales domestically.&#160;&#160;The remaining sales in both periods were exports to foreign countries.&#160;&#160;The accounts receivable balance of one customer represented approximately 16% of total accounts receivable at December 27
 2014
 and two customers represented a combined 25% of total accounts receivable at December 28
 2013. In addition
 a significant portion of the Company&#8217;s sales are to several key distributors
 which are large distribution companies with numerous divisions and subsidiaries who act independently. Such distributors as a group accounted for 43% and 45% of the Company&#8217;s net sales for the fiscal years ended December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013.


        
 -&#160;The majority of the Company&#8217;s accounts receivables are due from distributors (domestic and international) and retailers.&#160;&#160;Credit is extended based on evaluation of a customers&#8217; financial condition and
 generally
 collateral is not required. Accounts receivable are most often due within 30 to 90 days and are stated at amounts due from customers net of an allowance for doubtful accounts. Accounts outstanding longer than the contractual payment terms are considered past due. The Company determines its allowance by considering a number of factors
 including the length of time trade accounts receivable are past due
 the Company&#8217;s previous loss history
 the customer&#8217;s current ability to pay its obligation to the Company
 and the condition of the general economy and the industry as a whole. The Company writes-off accounts receivable when they become uncollectible
 and payments subsequently received on such receivables are credited to the bad debt expense. The Company does not accrue interest on accounts receivable past due.


        
&#160;- Deferred revenue represents amounts from sales of the Company&#8217;s product that have been billed and shipped
 but for which the transactions have not met its revenue recognition criteria.&#160;&#160;The cost of the related product has been recorded as deferred costs on its balance sheet.


        
        


        
&#160;- Inventory is stated at lower of cost or market determined by first in first out (FIFO) method.&#160;&#160;Inventories in excess of future demand are written down and charged to the provision for inventories.&#160;&#160;At the point of which loss is recognized
 a new
 lower cost basis for that inventory is established and subsequent changes in facts and circumstances do not result in the restoration or increase in the newly established cost basis.

The Company purchased approximately 26% and 27% of its finished products from one supplier and 28% and 28% of its finished products from another supplier during the periods ended&#160;December 27
 2014&#160;&#160;and December 28
 2013
 respectively.


        
&#160;- Deferred tax assets and liabilities are recognized for the future tax consequences attributable to differences between the financial statement carrying amounts of existing assets and liabilities and their respective tax bases.&#160;&#160;Deferred tax assets and liabilities are measured using enacted tax rates expected to apply to taxable income in the years in which those temporary differences are expected to be recovered or settled.&#160;&#160;The effect on deferred tax assets and liabilities of a change in tax rates is recognized in income in the period that includes the enactment date.&#160;&#160;A valuation allowance is recorded if there is uncertainty as to the realization of deferred tax assets. The Company will recognize a tax benefit in the financial statements for an uncertain tax position only if management&#8217;s assessment is that the position is &#8220;more likely than not&#8221; (i.e.
 a likelihood greater than 50 percent) to be allowed by the tax jurisdiction based solely on the technical merits of the position. The term &#8220;tax position&#8221; refers to a position in a previously filed tax return or a position expected to be taken in a future tax return that is reflected in measuring current or deferred income tax assets and liabilities for financial reporting purposes.

 -&#160;In May
 2014
 the FASB issued an accounting standards update that completes the joint effort by the FASB and International Accounting Standards Board to improve financial reporting by creating common revenue recognition guidance for GAAP and International Financial Reporting Standards. The update applies to all companies that enter into contracts with customers to transfer goods or services and is effective for Tofutti for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after December 15
 2015. Early application is not permitted and companies have the choice to apply the update either retrospectively to each reporting period presented or by recognizing the cumulative effect of applying the update at the date of initial application (January 1
 2017) and not adjusting comparative information. The Company is currently evaluating the requirements of this update and has not yet determined its impact on its financial statements.

In August
 2014
 the FASB issued guidance that requires management to evaluate whether there are conditions or events that raise substantial doubt about an entity&#8217;s ability to continue as a going concern. If such conditions or events exist
 disclosures are required that enable users of the financial statements to understand the nature of the conditions or events
 management&#8217;s evaluation of the circumstances and management&#8217;s plans to mitigate the conditions or events that raise substantial doubt about the entity&#8217;s ability to continue as a going concern. The Company will be required to perform an annual assessment of its ability to continue as a going concern when this standard becomes effective for it on October 1
 2017; however
 the adoption of this guidance is not expected to impact the Company&#8217;s financial position
 results of operations or cash flows.

The Company&#8217;s facilities are located in a one-story facility in Cranford
 New Jersey.&#160;&#160;The 6
200 square foot facility houses its administrative offices

 and a product development laboratory and test kitchen.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s original lease agreement expired on July 1

Disclosure Of Compensation Related Costs
 Share-Based Payments [Abstract]
        


        
        

On June 10
 2014
 the shareholders of the Company approved the 2014 Equity Incentive Plan (the &#8220;2014 Plan&#8221;). The 2014 Plan provides for grants of various types of awards that are designed to attract and retain highly qualified personnel who will contribute to the success of the Company and to provide incentives to participants in the 2014 Plan that are linked directly to increases in shareholder value which will therefore inure to the benefit of all shareholders of the Company. The Company intends to rely on a combination of multi-year performance awards
 options and other stock-based awards for these purposes.

The 2014 Plan made 250
000 shares of Common Stock available for awards. The 2014 Plan also permits performance-based 2014 awards paid under it to be tax deductible under Section 162(m) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986
 as amended
 as &#8220;performance-based compensation.&#8221;

There were no stock options granted in the last two fiscal years
 and no options were outstanding as of year-end
 December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013.

Management has concluded that based upon all available evidence it is more likely than not that deferred tax assets will not be utilized.&#160;&#160;The Company has recorded an increase in the&#160;&#160;valuation allowance in the amount of $69 during the year ended December 27
 2014. The remaining deferred tax asset is offset by the federal unrecorded tax benefit.

The Company will recognize a tax benefit in the financial statements for an uncertain tax position only if management&#8217;s assessment is that the position is &#8220;more likely than not&#8221; (i.e.
 a likelihood greater than 50 percent) to be allowed by the tax jurisdiction based solely on the technical merits of the position. The term &#8220;tax position&#8221; refers to a position in a previously filed tax return or a position expected to be taken in a future tax return that is reflected in measuring current or deferred income tax assets and liabilities for financial reporting purposes.

The following table indicates the changes to the Company&#8217;s uncertain tax positions for the fiscal years ended December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013:






















































The Company accounts for penalties or interest related to uncertain tax positions as part of its provision for income taxes. The Company had approximately $32 and $91 of accrued interest and penalties related to uncertain tax positions at December 27
 2014 and December 28
 2013
 respectively.&#160;&#160;The amount of uncertain tax positions that would affect the effective tax rate if they were recognized is $201.

The liability at December 27
 2014 for uncertain tax positions is included in accrued expenses.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s federal and state tax returns are open to examination for the years 2011 to 2014.
